glances:x:129:137::/var/lib/glances:/usr/sbin/nologin

							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Make an administrator user

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
First we are going to create a new user, who will not be an administrator at the beginning

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo adduser noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Añadiendo el usuario `noadmin' ...
Añadiendo el nuevo grupo `noadmin' (1001) ...
Añadiendo el nuevo usuario `noadmin' (1001) con grupo `noadmin' ...
Creando el directorio personal `/home/noadmin' ...
Copiando los ficheros desde `/etc/skel' ...
Nueva contraseña: 
Vuelva a escribir la nueva contraseña: 
passwd: contraseña actualizada correctamente
Cambiando la información de usuario para noadmin
Introduzca el nuevo valor, o presione INTRO para el predeterminado
	Nombre completo []: 
	Número de habitación []: 
	Teléfono del trabajo []: 
	Teléfono de casa []: 
	Otro []: 
¿Es correcta la información? [S/n] s

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Let's see which groups the user we just created is in, for this we use the command groups .

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!groups noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
noadmin : noadmin

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As we can see it is only in the noadmin group, which is a group that was created when creating the user

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Let's see which groups my user belongs to

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!groups wallabot

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
wallabot : wallabot adm cdrom sudo dip plugdev lpadmin lxd sambashare docker

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As we can see my user belongs to several other groups, among them to one called sudo. The users that have access to this group have administrator powers, so for the new user that we have created to have these powers we have to add him to the sudo group.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
To add a user to a group there are two ways, one is with the command gpasswd -a  .

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo gpasswd -a noadmin sudo

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Añadiendo al usuario noadmin al grupo sudo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Let us now see to which groups the user noadmin belongs to

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!groups noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
noadmin : noadmin sudo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As we can see, it already belongs to the sudo group, so it would already have administrator powers.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Remove the user noadmin from the sudo group with the command gpasswd -d  .

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo gpasswd -d noadmin sudo

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Eliminando al usuario noadmin del grupo sudo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We see that noadmin no longer belongs to the sudo group.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!groups noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
noadmin : noadmin

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
The second command to add a user to a group is usermod -aG  .

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo usermod -aG sudo noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Let's see again to which groups the user noadmin belongs to

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!groups noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
noadmin : noadmin sudo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We remove the user noadmin from the sudo group and delete it

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo gpasswd -d noadmin sudo

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Eliminando al usuario noadmin del grupo sudo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo userdel noadmin

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								

							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Command history

								
							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
history

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
If we enter the command history in the terminal we see a history of the commands used

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!history

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
 1009  docker build . nvidia/cuda
 1010  docker build --help
 1011  docker build --build-arg nvidia/cuda
 1012  docker build --build-arg [nvidia/cuda]
 1013  cd ../docker/
 1014  docker ps -a
 1015  docker rm boring_wescoff 
 1016  docker compose up -d
 1017  docker compose exec deepstream61 bash
 1018  cd ..
    ....
 1996  ps
 1997  ps aux
 1998  camerasIP.sh 
 1999  sudo su
 2000  sudo useradd usertest
 2001  sudo userdel usertest
 2002  sudo useradd usertest
 2003  sudo userdel usertest
 2004  sudo su
 2005  sudo apt install history
 2006  history
 2007  clear
 2008  history

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
If we want to execute one of the commands in the history, we do it through !, for example, if I want to execute again the command 1996

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
! !1996

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
    PID TTY          TIME CMD
   6610 pts/0    00:00:00 bash
  20826 pts/0    00:00:00 ps

							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
reverse-i-search

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
A more refined way to search the history is to enter CTRL+r, when doing this the following message will appear on the console

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!reverse-i-search)`':

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
So as you type, you will see commands that match what you have entered, for example, if I enter if, I get the last time I used ifconfig.

						

					

				

			

	
			

				

					

						

							
If we enter CTRL+r again, older occurrences will appear.

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Delete commands from history

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
There are commands like ls, cd, pwd that are not very useful to be in the history, so it can be configured so that they are not saved in the history. To do this we modify the file ~/.bashrc and add the line HISTIGNORE="pwd:ls:cd".

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Security

								
							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Fireward ufw

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Ubunut comes with the ufw fireward installed, but to check it we use the following command

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw status

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: inactivo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As we can see by default it is inactive, so we are going to create a set of rules. For example we are going to start by opening port 22 (SSH), for this we use the command sudo allow  comment "", with which we open a port and add a comment

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw allow 22 comment 'ssh'

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Regla añadida
Regla añadida (v6)

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As we can see you have opened port 22 for IPv4 and IPv6. We will now enable ufW with the command ufw enable.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw enable

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
El cortafuegos está activo y habilitado en el arranque del sistema

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
If we want to see the rules we have in the fireward we use the command ufw status.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw enable

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Hasta                      Acción      Desde
-----                      ------      -----
22                         ALLOW       Anywhere                   # ssh
22 (v6)                    ALLOW       Anywhere (v6)              # ssh

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We can also tell it to display the numbered rules with the command ufw status numbered.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw status numbered

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: activo
     Hasta                      Acción      Desde
     -----                      ------      -----
[ 1] 22                         ALLOW IN    Anywhere                   # ssh
[ 2] 22 (v6)                    ALLOW IN    Anywhere (v6)              # ssh

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As we have them numbered we can delete one by using the ufw delete  command, so to delete the rule for IPv6 we do the following

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw delete 2

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: activo
Borrando:
 allow 22 comment 'ssh'
¿Continuar con la operación (s|n)? s
Regla eliminada (v6)

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We return to the status

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw status numbered

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: activo
     Hasta                      Acción      Desde
     -----                      ------      -----
[ 1] 22                         ALLOW IN    Anywhere                   # ssh

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We see that rule number 2 has been effectively eliminated.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
If we want to enable the ssh connection from a single IP we use the flag from .

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw  allow from 192.168.1.103 proto tcp to any port 22 comment 'ssh ip'

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Regla añadida

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We recheck the rules

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw status numbered

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: activo
     Hasta                      Acción      Desde
     -----                      ------      -----
[ 1] 22                         ALLOW IN    Anywhere                   # ssh
[ 2] 22/tcp                     ALLOW IN    192.168.1.103              # ssh ip

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
If we want to delete all the rules we use the command reset.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw reset

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: activo
Reiniciando todas las reglas a sus valores predeterminados instalados.
¿Continuar con la operación (s|n)? s
Respaldando «user.rules» en «/etc/ufw/user.rules.20221205_171730»
Respaldando «before.rules» en «/etc/ufw/before.rules.20221205_171730»
Respaldando «after.rules» en «/etc/ufw/after.rules.20221205_171730»
Respaldando «user6.rules» en «/etc/ufw/user6.rules.20221205_171730»
Respaldando «before6.rules» en «/etc/ufw/before6.rules.20221205_171730»
Respaldando «after6.rules» en «/etc/ufw/after6.rules.20221205_171730»

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We recheck the status

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw status numbered

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: inactivo

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We see that there is no longer any rule

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
To disable the fireward we use the command ufw disable.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw disable

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
El cortafuegos está detenido y deshabilitado en el arranque del sistema

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We recheck the status

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo ufw status

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Estado: inactivo

							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Security auditing with Lynis.

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
To install Lynis you have to use the command sudo apt install lynis.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
To do an audit of your system you must use the lynis audit system command. This starts a scan of the entire system and reports back to you.

						

					

				

			

	
			

				

					

						

							
 > I am not going to show the result of my system scan so as not to show my vulnerabilities on the Internet.

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Command programming

								
							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Periodic command programming with cron.

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
With the cron command we can schedule commands to be executed periodically. To do this we have to edit the file /etc/crontab.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!cat /etc/crontab

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
# /etc/crontab: system-wide crontab
# Unlike any other crontab you don't have to run the `crontab'
# command to install the new version when you edit this file
# and files in /etc/cron.d. These files also have username fields,
# that none of the other crontabs do.
SHELL=/bin/sh
PATH=/usr/local/sbin:/usr/local/bin:/sbin:/bin:/usr/sbin:/usr/bin
# Example of job definition:
# .---------------- minute (0 - 59)
# |  .------------- hour (0 - 23)
# |  |  .---------- day of month (1 - 31)
# |  |  |  .------- month (1 - 12) OR jan,feb,mar,apr ...
# |  |  |  |  .---- day of week (0 - 6) (Sunday=0 or 7) OR sun,mon,tue,wed,thu,fri,sat
# |  |  |  |  |
# *  *  *  *  * user-name command to be executed
17 *	* * *	root    cd / && run-parts --report /etc/cron.hourly
25 6	* * *	root	test -x /usr/sbin/anacron || ( cd / && run-parts --report /etc/cron.daily )
47 6	* * 7	root	test -x /usr/sbin/anacron || ( cd / && run-parts --report /etc/cron.weekly )
52 6	1 * *	root	test -x /usr/sbin/anacron || ( cd / && run-parts --report /etc/cron.monthly )
#

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As you can see, in this file there are a series of commands that are executed periodically. The format of these commands is as follows

						

					

				

			

	
			

				

					

						

							
      .

						

					

				

			

	
	
	
			

				

					

						

							
To create well the date you want the command to be executed there are a lot of online pages that help you to write it well, like for example crontab guru

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Single run command scheduling with at

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
When we want a command to be executed in the future, but we do not want it to be done periodically, but only once, we can use the at command. For example, you turn on an azure machine, or Amazon, for which you are charged and you want to be sure that it will be turned off and you will not get a surprise in the bill, you can leave programmed that at night it will be turned off. This way, even if you forget to turn it off, it will turn itself off.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
We do an ls to the folder /tmp.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!ls -l /tmp

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
total 60
-rw------- 1 wallabot wallabot    0 sep 24 08:51 config-err-QM3AAe
-rw-r--r-- 1 root     root     2049 sep 24 08:51 glances-root.log
drwx------ 2 wallabot wallabot 4096 sep 24 09:06 pyright-9853-BG3nXEXw0Tao
drwxrwxr-x 3 wallabot wallabot 4096 sep 24 09:06 python-languageserver-cancellation
drwx------ 3 root     root     4096 sep 24 08:51 snap-private-tmp

drwx------ 3 root     root     4096 sep 24 08:51 systemd-private-371a1d9479324db8bd79b6844b8b589b-switcheroo-control.service-1QXRqj
drwx------ 3 root     root     4096 sep 24 08:51 systemd-private-371a1d9479324db8bd79b6844b8b589b-systemd-logind.service-lL35tg
drwx------ 3 root     root     4096 sep 24 08:51 systemd-private-371a1d9479324db8bd79b6844b8b589b-systemd-resolved.service-iaswSi

Now we are going to program a new file to be created in /tmp within 5 minutes

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!at 09:55 touch /tmp/at.txt

at> <EOT>

As we can see we must write at  and in the following line the command we want to be executed

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Now let's see the files in /tmp.

Keyboard shortcuts

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Below are a few shortcuts that are useful in the use of the terminal

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							

								
    
									
  • Ctrl+a: takes the cursor to the beginning of the command line.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+e: takes the cursor to the end of the command line.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+l: clears the terminal, similar to what the clear command does.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+u: clears from the cursor position to the beginning of the line. If you are at the end, it clears the entire line.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+k: clears from the cursor position to the end of the line. If you are at the beginning, it clears the entire line.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+h: does the same as the backspace key, deletes the character immediately preceding the cursor position.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+w: deletes the word immediately before the cursor.
    • 
									
  • Alt+d or Esc+d: deletes the next word after the cursor.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+p: sets the command line with the last command entered.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+r: starts the search for previously used commands, by typing part of a previously used command including options and parameters. A search is performed by pressing the key combination again to find previous matches.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+c: terminates the running process, useful for regaining control of the system.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+d: exits the terminal, similar to the exit command.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+z: suspends the execution of the running process and puts it in the background, with the fg command we can resume its execution.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+t: exchanges the position of the two characters before the cursor, useful for correcting mistyping.
    • 
									
  • Esc+t: exchanges the position of the two words before the cursor, useful for correcting mistyping.
    • 
									
  • Alt+f: moves the cursor to the beginning of the next word on the line, the same as Ctrl+right in the GNOME terminal.
    • 
									
  • Alt+b: moves the cursor to the beginning of the previous word on the line, the same as Ctrl+left in the GNOME terminal.
    • 
									
  • Tab: autocompletes commands or paths to directories or files.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+Shift+f: opens a dialog to do a text search in the terminal output.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+Shift+g: searches for the next occurrence of the previous search in the terminal.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+Shift+h: searches for the previous occurrence of the previous search in the terminal.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+Shift+c: copies the selected text from the terminal to the clipboard.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+Shift+v: paste the text from the clipboard into the command line.
    • 
									
  • Up: sets in the command line the previous command in the history, just like Ctrl+p.
    • 
									
  • Down: sets in the command line the next command in the history.
    • 
									
  • Left Mouse: selects lines of text from the terminal.
    • 
									
  • Ctrl+Left Mouse: selects terminal text blocks.

Fricadas

								
							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
You forgot to use sudo

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
Has it ever happened to you that you went to use a command that you were supposed to run with sudo, but you forgot to type sudo? Well, after receiving the corresponding error, if you do sudo !!, the previous command will be executed with sudo.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!apt update

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
Leyendo lista de paquetes... Hecho
[1;31mE: [0mNo se pudo abrir el fichero de bloqueo «/var/lib/apt/lists/lock» - open (13: Permiso denegado)[0m
[1;31mE: [0mNo se pudo bloquear el directorio /var/lib/apt/lists/[0m
[1;33mW: [0mSe produjo un problema al desligar el fichero /var/cache/apt/pkgcache.bin - RemoveCaches (13: Permiso denegado)[0m
[1;33mW: [0mSe produjo un problema al desligar el fichero /var/cache/apt/srcpkgcache.bin - RemoveCaches (13: Permiso denegado)[0m

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As you can see, doing sudo update gives us an error, but if we now run sudo !! it will run sudo apt update.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!sudo !!

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
[sudo] contraseña para wallabot: 

							

						

					

				

			

			
			

				

					

						

							

								
									
Kernel messages

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
With the dmesg command (display kernell ring buffer messages) we can see the kernel messages. For example, this is very useful to see if a USB device has been connected, or to debug HW errors of our computer.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!dmesg | tail

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
[   35.812312] input: LogiOps Virtual Input as /devices/virtual/input/input33
[   35.916406] input: LogiOps Virtual Input as /devices/virtual/input/input34
[   36.002064] input: LogiOps Virtual Input as /devices/virtual/input/input35
[   63.879806] input: MX Master 3 as /devices/virtual/misc/uhid/0005:046D:B023.0006/input/input36
[   63.879931] logitech-hidpp-device 0005:046D:B023.0006: input,hidraw3: BLUETOOTH HID v0.15 Keyboard [MX Master 3] on 4c:77:cb:1d:66:d0
[   63.902120] logitech-hidpp-device 0005:046D:B023.0006: HID++ 4.5 device connected.
[   69.604899] input: MX Keys Keyboard as /devices/virtual/misc/uhid/0005:046D:B35B.0007/input/input37
[   69.605221] input: MX Keys Mouse as /devices/virtual/misc/uhid/0005:046D:B35B.0007/input/input38
[   69.606204] hid-generic 0005:046D:B35B.0007: input,hidraw4: BLUETOOTH HID v0.13 Keyboard [MX Keys] on 4c:77:cb:1d:66:d0
[  188.285030] input: T9 (AVRCP) as /devices/virtual/input/input40

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
With the --follow flag we can see in real time the new messages that are generated.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
!dmesg --follow

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
^C

Cowsay

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
There is a command called cowsay to which you pass as a parameter a text and it draws a cow saying that text

						

					

				

			

	
			

				

					

						

							
It is possible that you do not have it installed, so to install it you have to enter the command

						

					

				

			

	
			

				

					

						

							
sudo apt install cowsay

						

					

				

			

	
	
			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
terminal("cowsay MaximoFN")

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
 __________
< MaximoFN >
 ----------
        \   ^__^
         \  (oo)\_______
            (__)\       )\/\
                ||----w |
                ||     ||

							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
If you add the flag -f dragon whoever says it is a dragon.

						

					

				

			

			

				

					
Code:

					

						

							

								
terminal("cowsay -f dragon MaximoFN")

								

							

						

					

				

				

					

						

							
Output:

							

								
 __________
< MaximoFN >

Cleaning

								
							

						

					

				

			

			

				

					

						

							
As the test folder has been created, we delete it to leave everything as we found it

!rm -r prueba
